                 <path fill="#21242C" d="M8.967 71.687l82.418 0q.735 0 1.274-.539t.539-1.274l0-42.973q-1.813 2.009-3.871 3.675-14.945 11.515-20.825 16.415t-7.693 6.272-4.851 2.695q-3.038 1.372-5.733 1.372l-.098 0q-2.695 0-5.733-1.372t-4.851-2.695q-1.813-1.372-7.693-6.272t-20.825-16.415q-2.058-1.666-3.871-3.675l0 42.973q0 .735.539 1.274t1.274.539zm84.231-62.034q0-2.499-1.813-2.499l-82.418 0q-.735 0-1.274.539t-.539 1.274q0 9.408 8.232 15.925 21.952 17.297 25.676 20.433 5.733 4.851 9.065 4.851l.098 0q2.254 0 5.194-2.009t7.056-5.537q11.662-9.261 22.491-17.738 3.038-2.401 5.635-6.468t2.597-7.399l0-1.372zm7.154-.686l0 60.907q0 3.675-2.646 6.321t-6.321 2.646l-82.418 0q-3.675 0-6.321-2.646t-2.646-6.321l0-60.907q0-3.675 2.646-6.321t6.321-2.646l82.418 0q3.675 0 6.321 2.646t2.646 6.321z" data-reactid="161"></path>

               <!-- react-text: 162 -->Email
               <!-- /react-text --></a>

           <div data-reactid="163">
            <div class="framework-perseus perseus-article bibliotron-article" data-reactid="164">
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="165">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="166">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="167">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="168">
                 <!-- react-text: 169 -->There are many different ways to sort. As selection sort runs, the subarray at the beginning of the array is sorted, but the subarray at the end is not. Selection sort scans the unsorted subarray for the next element to include in the sorted subarray.
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="170">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="171">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="172">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="173">
                 <!-- react-text: 174 -->Here's another way to think about sorting. Imagine that you are playing a card game. You're holding the cards in your hand, and these cards are sorted. The dealer hands you exactly one new card. You have to put it into the correct place so that the cards you're holding are still sorted. In selection sort, each element that you add to the sorted subarray is no smaller than the elements already in the sorted subarray. But in our card example, the new card could be smaller than some of the cards you're already holding, and so you go down the line, comparing the new card against each card in your hand, until you find the place to put it. You insert the new card in the right place, and once again, your hand holds fully sorted cards. Then the dealer gives you another card, and you repeat the same procedure. Then another card, and another card, and so on, until the dealer stops giving you cards.
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="175">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="176">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="177">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="178">
                 <!-- react-text: 179 -->This is the idea behind 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <strong data-reactid="180">
                  <!-- react-text: 181 -->insertion sort
                  <!-- /react-text --></strong>
                 <!-- react-text: 182 -->. Loop over positions in the array, starting with index 1. Each new position is like the new card handed to you by the dealer, and you need to insert it into the correct place in the sorted subarray to the left of that position. Here's a visualization that steps through that:
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="183">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="184">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="185">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="186">
                 <div class="perseus-widget-container widget-nohighlight widget-block" data-reactid="187">
                  <iframe sandbox="allow-popups allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation" src="https://www.khanacademy.org/computer-programming/program/5008603698429952/embedded?embed=yes&amp;author=no&amp;editor=no&amp;buttons=no&amp;settings=%7B%7D" style="height:400px;width:402px;" class="perseus-scratchpad" allowfullscreen data-reactid="188"></iframe>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="189">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="190">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="191">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="192">
                 <!-- react-text: 193 -->In terms of arrays, imagine that the subarray from index 0 through index 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <span style="white-space:nowrap;" data-reactid="194"><span data-reactid="195"></span><span data-reactid="196"><span data-reactid="197"></span><span aria-hidden="true" data-reactid="198"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml">

                        </annotation>
                       </semantics>
                      </math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="strut" style="height:0.64444em;"></span><span class="strut bottom" style="height:0.64444em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="base textstyle uncramped"><span class="mord mathrm">5</span></span></span></span></span><span style="border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px;" data-reactid="199">5</span></span><span data-reactid="200"></span></span>
                 <!-- react-text: 201 --> is already sorted, and we want to insert the element currently in index 6 into this sorted subarray, so that the subarray from index 0 through index 6 is sorted. Here's how we start:
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="202">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="203">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="204">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="205">
                 <div class="perseus-widget-container widget-nohighlight widget-block" data-reactid="206">

                 <!-- react-text: 220 -->And here's what the subarray should look like when we're done:

             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="221">

                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="224">
                 <div class="perseus-widget-container widget-nohighlight widget-block" data-reactid="225">
                  <div class="perseus-image-widget" data-reactid="226">

               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="490">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="491">
                 <div class="perseus-widget-container widget-nohighlight widget-block" data-reactid="492">
                  <div class="perseus-image-widget" data-reactid="493">
                   <div class="fixed-to-responsive svg-image" style="max-width:163px;max-height:74px;" data-reactid="494">
                    <div style="padding-bottom:45.4%;" data-reactid="495"></div>
                    <span style="background:url(/images/spinner.gif) no-repeat;background-position:center;width:100%;height:100%;position:absolute;min-width:20px;" data-reactid="496"></span>
                   </div>
                   <span class="perseus-sr-only" data-reactid="497">
                    <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="498">
                     <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="499">
                      <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="500">
                       <!-- react-text: 501 -->Insertion sort
                       <!-- /react-text -->
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div></span>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="502">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="503">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="504">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="505">
                 <!-- react-text: 506 -->A couple of situations that came up in our example bear a little more scrutiny: when the key being inserted is less than all elements to its left (as when we inserted keys 2 and 3), and when it's greater than or equal to all elements to its left (as when we inserted key 13). In the former case, every element in the subarray to the left of the key slides one position to the right, and we have to stop once we've run off the left end of the array. In the latter case, the first time we compare the key with an element to its left, we find that the key is already in its correct position relative to all elements to its left; no elements slide over and the key drops back into the position in which it started.
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="507">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="508">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="509">
                <h3 data-reactid="510">
                 <!-- react-text: 511 -->Inserting a value into a sorted subarray
                 <!-- /react-text --></h3>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="512">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="513">
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="514">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="515">
                 <!-- react-text: 516 -->The main step in insertion sort is making space in an array to put the current value, which is stored in the variable 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <code data-reactid="517">key</code>
                 <!-- react-text: 518 -->. As we saw above, we go through the subarray to the left of 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <code data-reactid="519">key</code>
                 <!-- react-text: 520 -->'s initial position, right to left, sliding each element that is greater than 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <code data-reactid="521">key</code>
                 <!-- react-text: 522 --> one position to the right. Once we find an element that is less than 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <code data-reactid="523">key</code>
                 <!-- react-text: 524 -->, or equal to 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <code data-reactid="525">key</code>
                 <!-- react-text: 526 -->, we stop sliding and copy 
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                 <code data-reactid="527">key</code>
                 <!-- react-text: 528 --> into the vacated position just to the right of this element. (Of course, the position is not truly vacated, but its element was slid over to the right.) This diagram shows the idea:
                 <!-- /react-text -->
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="529">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="530">
               <div class="paragraph perseus-paragraph-centered" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="531"> 
               </div>
               <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="1" data-reactid="532">
                <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="533">
                 <div class="perseus-widget-container widget-nohighlight widget-block" data-reactid="534">
                  <div class="perseus-image-widget" data-reactid="535">
                   <div class="fixed-to-responsive svg-image" style="max-width:361px;max-height:395px;" data-reactid="536">
                    <div style="padding-bottom:109.42%;" data-reactid="537"></div>
                    <span style="background:url(/images/spinner.gif) no-repeat;background-position:center;width:100%;height:100%;position:absolute;min-width:20px;" data-reactid="538"></span>
                   </div>
                   <span class="perseus-sr-only" data-reactid="539">
                    <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="540">
                     <div class="paragraph" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="541">
                      <div class="paragraph" data-reactid="542">
                       <!-- react-text: 543 -->Insertion
                       <!-- /react-text -->
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div></span>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="clearfix" data-reactid="544">
              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="545">
               <div class="paragraph perseus-paragraph-centered" data-perseus-paragraph-index="0" data-reactid="546">
                <hr data-reactid="547">
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>

              <div class="perseus-renderer perseus-renderer-responsive" data-reactid="549">

As selection sort runs, the subarray at the beginning of the array is sorted, but the subarray at the end is not. Selection sort scans the unsorted subarray for the next element to include in the sorted subarray.\",\"images\":{},\"widgets\":{}},{\"content\":\"Here's another way to think about sorting. Imagine that you are playing a card game. You're holding the cards in your hand, and these cards are sorted. The dealer hands you exactly one new card. You have to put it into the correct place so that the cards you're holding are still sorted. In selection sort, each element that you add to the sorted subarray is no smaller than the elements already in the sorted subarray. But in our card example, the new card could be smaller than some of the cards you're already holding, and so you go down the line, comparing the new card against each card in your hand, until you find the place to put it. You insert the new card in the right place, and once again, your hand holds fully sorted cards. Then the dealer gives you another card, and you repeat the same procedure. Then another card, and another card, and so on, until the dealer stops giving you cards.\",\"images\":{},\"widgets\":{}},{\"content\":\"This is the idea behind **insertion sort**. match(additionalAssert7P),match(additionalAssert8P),match(additionalAssert9P)\n                                        );\n     \n    var result= allPass(additionalAssertMatch);\n    \n   \n    /****************************\n    *Passing Code with Exceptions \n    *****************************/\n   \n    /** check that the additional assert is unique and uses an unsorted array**/\n    \n    //compares an ArrayExpression to an array\n    //(faster than converting to strings and comparing the strings)\n    var isSameArray=function(ArrayExpression, array){\n        if(ArrayExpression.elements.length !== array.length){\n            return false;\n        }\n        for(var i=0; i< array.length;i++){\n            if(ArrayExpression.elements[i].value !== array[i]){\n                return false;\n            }\n        }\n        return true;\n    };\n    \n    //checks that an ArrayExpression is unsorted\n    //(faster than joining, sorting then comparing)\n    var isUnsorted=function(ArrayExpression){\n        for(var i=1; i< ArrayExpression.elements.length;i++){\n            if(ArrayExpression.elements[i-1].value > ArrayExpression.elements[i].value){\n                return true;\n            }\n        }\n        return false;\n    }\n    \n    \n    var literalArrayConstraint = constraint([\"$literalArray\"],function(literalArray){\n        return (literalArray.type === \"ArrayExpression\") && !isSameArray(literalArray,[22, 11, 99, 88, 9, 7, 42]) && isUnsorted(literalArray);\n    });\n    \n    var additionalUniqueAssert1S= structure(additionalAssert1P,literalArrayConstraint);\n    var additionalUniqueAssert2S= It just calls `insert` on the elements at indices $ 1, 2, 3, \\\\ldots, n-1 $. Just as each call to `indexOfMinimum` took an amount of time that depended on the size of the sorted subarray, so does each call to `insert`. Actually, the word \\\"does\\\" in the previous sentence should be \\\"can,\\\" and we'll see why.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"Let's take a situation where we call `insert` and the value being inserted into a subarray is less than every element in the subarray. For example, if we're inserting 0 into the subarray [2, 3, 5, 7, 11], then every element in the subarray has to slide over one position to the right. So, in general, if we're inserting into a subarray with $ k $ elements, all $ k $ might have to slide over by one position. Rather than counting exactly how many lines of code we need to test an element against a key and slide the element, let's agree that it's a constant number of lines; let's call that constant $ c $. Therefore, it could take up to $ c \\\\cdot k $ lines to insert into a subarray of $ k $ elements.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"Suppose that upon every call to `insert`, the value being inserted is less than every element in the subarray to its left. When we call `insert` the first time, $ k=1 $. The second time, $ k=2 $. The third time, $ k=3 $. And so on, up through the last time, when $ k = n-1 $. Therefore, the total time spent inserting into sorted subarrays is  \\n\\n$ c \\\\cdot 1 + c \\\\cdot 2 + c \\\\cdot 3 + \\\\cdots c \\\\cdot (n-1) = c \\\\cdot (1 + 2 + 3 + \\\\cdots + (n-1)) $ .  \\n\\nThat sum is an arithmetic series, except that it goes up to $ n-1 $ rather than $ n $. Using our formula for arithmetic series, we get that the total time spent inserting into sorted subarrays is  \\n\\n$ c \\\\cdot (n-1+1)((n-1)/2) = cn^2/2 - cn/2 $ .  \\n\\nUsing big-\\u0398 notation, we discard the low-order term $ cn/2 $ and the constant factors $ c $ and 1/2, getting the result that the running time of insertion sort, in this case, is $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"Can insertion sort take _less_ than $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $ time? The answer is yes. Suppose we have the array [2, 3, 5, 7, 11], where the sorted subarray is the first four elements, and we're inserting the value 11\\\\. Upon the first test, we find that 11 is greater than 7, and so no elements in the subarray need to slide over to the right. Then this call of `insert` takes just constant time. Suppose that _every_ call of `insert` takes constant time. Because there are $ n-1 $ calls to `insert`, if each call takes time that is some constant $ c $, then the total time for insertion sort is $ c \\\\cdot (n-1) $, which is $ \\\\Theta(n) $, not $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"Can either of these situations occur? Can each call to `insert` cause every element in the subarray to slide one position to the right? Can each call to `insert` cause no elements to slide? The answer is yes to both questions. A call to `insert` causes every element to slide over if the key being inserted is less than every element to its left. So, if every element is less than every element to its left, the running time of insertion sort is $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $. What would it mean for every element to be less than the element to its left? The array would have to start out in _reverse_ sorted order, such as [11, 7, 5, 3, 2]. So a reverse-sorted array is the worst case for insertion sort.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"How about the opposite case? A call to `insert` causes no elements to slide over if the key being inserted is greater than or equal to every element to its left. So, if every element is greater than or equal to every element to its left, the running time of insertion sort is $ \\\\Theta(n) $. This situation occurs if the array starts out already sorted, and so an already-sorted array is the best case for insertion sort.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"What else can we say about the running time of insertion sort? Suppose that the array starts out in a random order. Then, on average, we'd expect that each element is less than half the elements to its left. In this case, on average, a call to `insert` on a subarray of $ k $ elements would slide $ k/2 $ of them. The running time would be half of the worst-case running time. But in asymptotic notation, where constant coefficients don't matter, the running time in the average case would still be $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $, just like the worst case.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"What if you knew that the array was \\\"almost sorted\\\": every element starts out at most some constant number of positions, say 17, from where it's supposed to be when sorted? Then each call to `insert` slides at most 17 elements, and the time for one call of `insert` on a subarray of $ k $ elements would be at most $ 17 \\\\cdot c $. Over all $ n-1 $ calls to `insert`, the running time would be $ 17 \\\\cdot c \\\\cdot (n-1) $, which is $ \\\\Theta(n) $, just like the best case. So insertion sort is fast when given an almost-sorted array.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"To sum up the running times for insertion sort:\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"*   Worst case: $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $.\\n*   Best case: $ \\\\Theta(n) $.\\n*   Average case for a random array: $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $.\\n*   \\\"Almost sorted\\\" case: $ \\\\Theta(n) $.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"If you had to make a blanket statement that applies to all cases of insertion sort, you would have to say that it runs in $ O(n^2) $ time. You cannot say that it runs in $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $ time in all cases, since the best case runs in $ \\\\Theta(n) $ time. And you cannot say that it runs in $ \\\\Theta(n) $ time in all cases, since the worst-case running time is $ \\\\Theta(n^2) $.\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"* * *\", \"images\": {}, \"widgets\": {}}, {\"content\": \"This content is a collaboration of [Dartmouth Computer Science](http://www.cs.dartmouth.edu/) professors [Thomas Cormen](http://www.cs.dartmouth.edu/~thc/) and [Devin Balkcom](http://www.cs.dartmouth.edu/~devin/), plus the Khan Academy computing curriculum team.
